  192. This is a great old school scent. What does it smell like? The short answer is &#34;barbershop&#34;, as in you'll smell like you do right after a haircut. This is because even many unisex salons typically finish a haircut with Pinaud's talcum powder, and this has some of the same smell. More specifically, I can smell citrus oil (not so much lemon blossom or orange oil as citronella), and J&J baby powder, plus there's also a &#34;bass note&#34; that comes from tree moss, but I only really smell that separately in the bottle. I never disliked the scent but it took a day or two for me to really get used to it, and really love it. This is a strong smell by the way. If you put a little on your shoulders, behind your ears, and on your wrist you won't need a separate cologne, and it will last all day. How does it work as an aftershave by the way? On me personally, its excellent (my skin is pretty sensitive but also a bit oily which is why I seem to get along well with &#34;splash&#34; aftershaves). I can definitely feel when I put it on, but it doesn't sting... much. Some seem to think its quite strong in that regard, I don't, I think its moderately strong. Once the slight sting subsides, it leaves my skin feeling very good (better than a lot of inexpensive aftershaves like Brut or Aqua Velva, specifically this leaves my skin soft and moist without feeling sticky), so I'm a fan in that regard. There are two other things that this product is famous for. 1, It's supposed to make you &#34;smell like a man&#34;. This is the reason a lot of people say they use the stuff. Frankly, that claim usually worries me a bit because who's to say what &#34;a man&#34; smells like or if he smells &#34;good&#34;? Seriously, I read that and I always worry I might be buying extra strength splash on B.O. Every once in a while a fragrance designer will screw up and actually do this. I've accidentally bought a deodorant that made me smell exactly like I just got out of an extra long gym class andFORGOT my deodorant. Anyway this smells &#34;pleasant&#34; and makes you smell &#34;clean&#34; without being flowery, sweet, or fruity which is what I'm personally after. The second thing Pinaud is known for is making you smell, &#34;like an old guy&#34;. Is it popular with senior citizens? Sure. But Pinaud also implies that this formula dates from 1810, and if you look up the fragrance ingredients a lot of them double as an insect repellent or even a remedy for lice or mites, its likely that the formula really is around 200 years old, which means it was also probably popular with old guys when my grandfather's grandfather was just a kid. It's still around because its a classic. Oh and the best part is this stuff is extremely inexpensive and widely available. The price you see here is also the price you pay at your local Wal-Greens. So for $6 for around 6 oz you have a great, classic, distinctive scent, and a good quality aftershave that can double as your cologne. This stuff is a true bargain but I removed the word &#34;cheap&#34; from my review because while this is inexpensive, not &#34;cheap&#34; as either a fragrance or an aftershave. It works great, and smells great. This is not my absolute favorite fragrance (Muelhen's 4711 is my very favorite), and its not my very favorite Pinaud product (I like the Vanilla Clubman even better) but I love this stuff and I also love the fact that its readily available in any drug store or supermarket, which made it my personal go-to for a while. However its fallen off that list of late because there is one problem with a distinctive unusual aftershave that's strong smelling enough to double as a cologne: it s a jealous master that will fight any actual cologne you may want to wear. When I decided spray on colognes were generally easier and more convenient than having my splash-on aftershave pull double duty, ended up using the regular clubman a lot less often. For this reason I've subsequently deducted a star as well. If youwant to smell like this alone, it would be five stars. Although this works fantastically as an aftershave, and I'll probably never be without a bottle, this is definitely below 4711 Aftershave and Pinaud's Vanilla Clubman for me personally now, because they do a better job of letting my spray cologne (usually Azzaro Pour Homme or Cerruti 1881) do its job.

You want a glycerin-based product. My favorite is George F. Trumper brand \\"skin food\\" (especially this one: [[ASIN:B0007M3ZKI Geo F. Trumper Limes Skin Food, 100ml]]). These products cost a bit more, but are dramatically better at soothing your skin after shaving. Any alcohol-based \\"lotion\\" will sting, and something like the Trumper skin food does not (it's actually so soothing I occasionally use it on the patches of eczema I develop on my arms in the driest part of winter). If you shave with a brush, good shaving cream or soap (NOT FOAM OR GEL FROM A CAN, but something from a tube or tub, of which there are numerous options), and a good blade (honestly, old-school double-edged safety razors are far superior to so-called \\"modern\\" cartridge razors), and if you use skin food afterward, you'll get the best shave possible. With that strategy, and by shaving in the shower with lots of hot water, I can get a shave that is even better than a barbershop straight-razor shave.<br /><br />Back to the actual product being reviewed, though--if your skin isn't significantly irritated, or if you're really going to use aftershave as a cologne, not applying it right after shaving, this is a nice option. It's pleasant, but not overly strong, and in the proper context I do recommend it.

  523. Over the last year or so, I have bought and used five different after shave lotions - Lucky Tiger, Proraso, Pinaud Clubman, and Captain's Choice (Bay Rum and Sandalwood). Depending on my mood, I used one or the other, so my comparison has been somewhat continuous. Overall, they are all excellent, however, they are naturally different in various ways, so one's taste may cause a preference for one or the other.<br /><br />Lucky Tiger is the least astringent. You don't get that cooling sensation. It's probably the most like a skin conditioner. Although its label says &#34;with Aloe Vera&#34;, its other ingredients are not listed. Its aloe vera plus I suspect witch hazel are what make me say it is most like a skin conditioner. I don't think it has any alcohol. So if you're most concerned about keeping your face smooth and soft over the long run, you might prefer Lucky Tiger.<br /><br />The others all have alcohol and give you that familiar cooling, fresh, astringent sensation. I would say that Pinaud Clubman is the most astringent and cooling, followed by Proraso, Clubman's Bay Rum, and Clubman's Sandalwood. It's hard to say there is a difference between the two Clubman's varieties. The coolness of Proraso is minty and lingers a little longer.<br /><br />I don't believe in giving a product a poor review because it doesn't meet a personal preference (for example scent or astringency in an after shave). Therefore, I would rate them all as five stars.<br /><br />My preference is Pinaud Clubman because I like a cool feeling on my face after a shave. Also, when an after shave causes any razor burns and minor cuts to sting, I feel like I am doing something positive to treat them, even if another after shave might help them heal better without your feeling anything. Lack of stinging indicates fewer burns and cuts meaning that I've given myself a good shave. So, the more astringency the better for me. As a bonus, Pinaud Clubman is the lowest cost.
